         Improperia
        </a>
        ("Reproaches") with the
        <a href="/wiki/Trisagion" title="Trisagion">
         Trisagion
        </a>
        hymn are chanted.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
         <a href="#cite_note-38">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Holy Communion
        </b>
        is done according to a rite based on that of the final part of Mass, beginning with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord's Prayer">
         Our Father
        </a>
        , but omitting the ceremony of "
        <a href="/wiki/Fraction_(religion)" title="Fraction (religion)">
         Breaking of the Bread
        </a>
        " and its related chant, the "
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agnus_Dei" title="Agnus Dei">
         Agnus Dei
        </a>
        ". The
        <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">
         Eucharist
        </a>
        , consecrated at the Evening Mass of the Lord's Supper on
        <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">
         Holy Thursday
        </a>
        , is distributed at this service.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
         <a href="#cite_note-39">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Before the reform of
        <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">
         Pope Pius XII
        </a>
        , only the priest received Communion in the framework of what was called the "
        <a href="/wiki/Mass_of_the_Presanctified" title="Mass of the Presanctified">
         Mass of the Presanctified
        </a>
        ", which included the usual Offertory prayers, with the placing of wine in the chalice, but which omitted the
        <a href="/wiki/Canon_of_the_Mass" title="Canon of the Mass">
         Canon of the Mass
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanctamissa.org_31-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-sanctamissa.org-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The priest and people then depart in silence, and the altar cloth is removed, leaving the altar bare except for the crucifix and two or four candlesticks.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
         <a href="#cite_note-40">
          [40]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stations_of_the_Cross">
        Stations of the Cross
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Stations of the Cross">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg/170px-GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg/255px-GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg/340px-GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GoodFr_CroosWay_Colloseo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Way_of_the_Cross" title="Way of the Cross">
          Way of the Cross
         </a>
         , celebrated at the
         <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">
          Colosseum
         </a>
         in Rome on Good Friday
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG/220px-Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG/330px-Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG/440px-Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canopy_erected_at_the_Temple_of_Venus_and_Rome_during_Good_Friday_ceremonies.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rome: canopy erected at the "Temple of Venus and Rome" during the "Way of the Cross" ceremony
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In addition to the prescribed
       <a href="/wiki/Liturgy" title="Liturgy">
        liturgical
       </a>
       service, the
       <a href="/wiki/Stations_of_the_Cross" title="Stations of the Cross">
        Stations of the Cross
       </a>
       are often prayed either in the church or outside, and a prayer service may be held from midday to 3.00 pm, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Three_Hours%27_Agony" title="Three Hours' Agony">
        Three Hours' Agony
       </a>
       . In countries such as Malta, Italy, Philippines, Puerto Rico and Spain, processions with statues representing the Passion of Christ are held.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In Rome, since the papacy of Saint
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Paul_II" title="John Paul II">
        John Paul II
       </a>
       , the heights of the
       <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Venus_and_Roma" title="Temple of Venus and Roma">
        Temple of Venus and Roma
       </a>
       and their position opposite the main entrance to the Colosseum have been used to good effect as a public address platform. This may be seen in the photograph below where a red canopy has been erected to shelter the Pope as well as an illuminated cross, on the occasion of the
       <b>
        Way of the Cross
       </b>
       ceremony. The Pope, either personally or through a representative, leads the faithful through meditations on the stations of the cross while a cross is carried from there to the Colosseum.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In Polish churches, a tableau of Christ's Tomb is unveiled in the sanctuary. Many of the faithful spend long hours into the night grieving at the Tomb, where it is customary to kiss the wounds on the Lord's body. A life-size figure of Jesus lying in his tomb is widely visited by the faithful, especially on Holy Saturday. The tableaux may include flowers, candles, figures of angels standing watch, and the three crosses atop Mt Calvary, and much more. Each parish strives to come up with the most artistically and religiously evocative arrangement in which the Blessed Sacrament, draped in a filmy veil, is prominently displayed.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Acts_of_Reparation_to_Jesus_Christ">
        Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation_to_Jesus_Christ" title="Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ">
        Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="951" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg/170px-Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg/255px-Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg/340px-Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christ_Carrying_the_Cross_1580.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">
          El Greco
         </a>
         's
         <i>
          Jesus Carrying the Cross
         </i>
         , 1580
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Roman Catholic tradition includes specific prayers and devotions as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_reparation" title="Acts of reparation">
         acts of reparation
        </a>
       </i>
       for the sufferings and insults that Jesus suffered during his Passion on Good Friday. These Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ do not involve a petition for a beneficiary, but aim to "repair the sins" against Jesus. Some such prayers are provided in the
       <a href="/wiki/Raccolta" title="Raccolta">
        Raccolta
       </a>
       Catholic prayer book (approved by a Decree of 1854, and published by the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
        Holy See
       </a>
       in 1898) which also includes prayers as
       <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation_to_the_Virgin_Mary" title="Acts of Reparation to the Virgin Mary">
        Acts of Reparation to the Virgin Mary
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In his encyclical
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Miserentissimus_Redemptor" title="Miserentissimus Redemptor">
         Miserentissimus Redemptor
        </a>
       </i>
       on reparations,
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">
        Pope Pius XI
       </a>
       called Acts of Reparation to Jesus Christ a duty for Catholics and referred to them as "some sort of compensation to be rendered for the injury" with respect to the sufferings of Jesus.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
        Pope John Paul II
       </a>
       referred to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation" title="Acts of Reparation">
        Acts of Reparation
       </a>
       as the "unceasing effort to stand beside the endless crosses on which the Son of God continues to be crucified".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Anglican_Communion">
        Anglican Communion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Anglican Communion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The 1662
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Common_Prayer" title="Book of Common Prayer">
        Book of Common Prayer
       </a>
       did not specify a particular rite to be observed on Good Friday but local custom came to mandate an assortment of services, including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seven_Last_Words_from_the_Cross" title="Seven Last Words from the Cross">
        Seven Last Words from the Cross
       </a>
       and a three-hour service consisting of
       <a href="/wiki/Matins" title="Matins">
        Matins
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">
        Ante-communion
       </a>
       (using the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reserved_Sacrament" title="Reserved Sacrament">
        Reserved Sacrament
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/High_church" title="High church">
        high church
       </a>
       parishes) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evening_Prayer_(Book_of_Common_Prayer)" title="Evening Prayer (Book of Common Prayer)">
        Evensong
       </a>
       . In recent times,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2017)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       revised editions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Common_Prayer" title="Book of Common Prayer">
        Prayer Book
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Common_Worship" title="Common Worship">
        Common Worship
       </a>
       have re-introduced pre-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">
        Reformation
       </a>
       forms of observance of Good Friday corresponding to those in today's Roman Catholic Church, with special nods to the rites that had been observed in the Church of England prior to the
       <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">
        Henrican, Edwardian and Elizabethan reforms
       </a>
       , including Creeping to the Cross.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lutheran_Church">
        Lutheran Church
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Lutheran Church">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4656" data-file-width="2620" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg/220px-Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg/330px-Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg/440px-Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chancel_of_Grace_Lutheran_Church_on_Good_Friday.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Chancel" title="Chancel">
          chancel
         </a>
         of this Lutheran church is adorned with black
         <a href="/wiki/Parament" title="Parament">
          paraments
         </a>
         on Good Friday, the liturgical colour associated with Good Friday in the Lutheran Churches.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">
        Lutheran
       </a>
       tradition from the 16th to the 20th century, Good Friday was the most important religious holiday, and abstention from all worldly works was expected. During that time, Lutheranism had no restrictions on the celebration of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">
        Eucharist
       </a>
       on Good Friday; on the contrary, it was a prime day on which to receive the Eucharist, and services were often accentuated by special music such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/St_Matthew_Passion" title="St Matthew Passion">
         St Matthew Passion
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">
        Johann Sebastian Bach
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GassmannOldenburg2011_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GassmannOldenburg2011-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       More recently, Lutheran liturgical practice has recaptured Good Friday as part of the larger sweep of the great Three Days: Maundy Thursday, Good Friday, and the Vigil of Easter. The Three Days remain one liturgy which celebrates the death and resurrection of Jesus. As part of the liturgy of the Three Days, Lutherans generally fast from the Eucharist on Good Friday. Rather, it is celebrated in remembrance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Last_Supper" title="Last Supper">
        Last Supper
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">
        Maundy Thursday
       </a>
       and at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vigil_of_Easter" title="Vigil of Easter">
        Vigil of Easter
       </a>
       . One practice among Lutheran churches is to celebrate a
       <a href="/wiki/Tenebrae" title="Tenebrae">
        tenebrae
       </a>
       service on Good Friday, typically conducted in candlelight and consisting of a collection of passion accounts from the four gospels. While being called "Tenebrae" it holds little resemblance to the now-suppressed Catholic monastic rite of the same name.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Good Friday liturgy appointed in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Worship" title="Evangelical Lutheran Worship">
         Evangelical Lutheran Worship
        </a>
       </i>
       , the worship book of the Evangelical Lutheran Church in America, specifies a liturgy similar to the revised Roman Catholic liturgy. A rite for adoration of the crucified Christ includes the optional singing of the Solemn Reproaches in an updated and revised translation which eliminates some of the anti-Jewish overtones in previous versions. Influenced by the ecumenical liturgical renewal movement and in an attempt to recover patterns of worship from the early church, many Lutheran congregations are moving away from long preaching services centered on a dramatic and sentimentalized remembrance of the "Seven Last Words," sayings of Jesus assembled from the four gospels, toward a more devotional practice that places an emphasis on the triumph of the cross, and a singular biblical account of the Passion narrative from the Gospel of John.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Along with observing a general Lenten fast,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GassmannOldenburg2011_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-GassmannOldenburg2011-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       many Lutherans emphasize the importance of Good Friday as a day of fasting within the kalendar.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pfatteicher1990_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pfatteicher1990-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JacobsHaas1899_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-JacobsHaas1899-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        A Handbook for the Discipline of Lent
       </i>
       recommends the Lutheran guideline to "Fast on Ash Wednesday and Good Friday with only one simple meal during the day, usually without meat".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ELCA1978_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ELCA1978-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_mainstream_Protestant_traditions">
        Other mainstream Protestant traditions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Other mainstream Protestant traditions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4032" data-file-width="3024" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e6/Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg/220px-Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e6/Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg/330px-Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e6/Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg/440px-Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Minister_prostrates_at_the_start_of_United_Methodist_Good_Friday_liturgy.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A United Methodist minister
         <a href="/wiki/Prostration" title="Prostration">
          prostrates
         </a>
         at the start of the Good Friday liturgy at Holy Family Church, in accordance with the rubrics in the
         <a href="/wiki/The_United_Methodist_Book_of_Worship_(1992)" title="The United Methodist Book of Worship (1992)">
          Book of Worship
         </a>
         . The
         <a href="/wiki/Processional_cross" title="Processional cross">
          processional cross
         </a>
         is veiled in black, the liturgical colour associated with Good Friday in Methodist Churches.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1960" data-file-width="4032" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3b/Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg/350px-Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3b/Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg/525px-Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3b/Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg/700px-Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chancel_of_Houston_Memorial_UMC_on_Good_Friday.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         On Maundy Thursday, the
         <a href="/wiki/Stripping_of_the_Altar" title="Stripping of the Altar">
          altar of this Methodist church was stripped
         </a>
         and the crucifix of this Methodist church has been veiled in black for Good Friday (black is the liturgical colour for Good Friday in the United Methodist Church). A wooden cross sits in front of the bare chancel for the veneration of the cross ceremony, which occurs during the United Methodist Good Friday liturgy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many other mainstream
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant
       </a>
       communities hold special services on this day as well.
       <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">
        Moravians
       </a>
       hold a
       <a href="/wiki/Lovefeast" title="Lovefeast">
        Lovefeast
       </a>
       on Good Friday as they receive Holy Communion on
       <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">
        Maundy Thursday
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">
        Methodist Church
       </a>
       commemorates Good Friday with
       <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">
        fasting
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaysWacker2010_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BaysWacker2010-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_of_worship" title="Service of worship">
        service of worship
       </a>
       , often based on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seven_Last_Words_from_the_Cross" title="Seven Last Words from the Cross">
        Seven Last Words from the Cross
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reflector-Good_Friday_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Reflector-Good_Friday-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UMC-Good_Friday_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UMC-Good_Friday-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is not uncommon for some communities to hold interdenominational services on Good Friday.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed" title="Reformed">
        Reformed
       </a>
       tradition, Good Friday is one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_feast" title="Evangelical feast">
        evangelical feasts
       </a>
       and is thus widely observed with
       <a href="/wiki/Church_service" title="Church service">
        church services
       </a>
       , which feature the Solemn Reproaches in the pattern of
       <a href="/wiki/Psalm_78" title="Psalm 78">
        Psalm 78
       </a>
       , towards the end of the liturgy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Associated_customs">
        Associated customs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Associated customs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="2500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg/220px-Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg/330px-Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg/440px-Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Good_Friday_in_St._Pius_X_Church.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Good Friday service in Ireland
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In many countries with a strong Christian tradition such as Australia, Bermuda, Brazil, Canada, the countries of the Caribbean, Chile, Colombia, Costa Rica, Czech Republic, Ecuador, Finland, Germany, Hungary, Malta, Mexico, New Zealand,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Peru, the Philippines, the Scandinavian countries, Singapore, Spain, Switzerland, the United Kingdom, and Venezuela, the day is observed as a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_holidays_by_country" title="List of holidays by country">
        public or federal holiday
       </a>
       . In the United States, 12 states observe Good Friday as state holiday: Connecticut, Texas, Delaware, Hawaii, Indiana, Tennessee, Florida, Kentucky, Louisiana, New Jersey, North Carolina and North Dakota. Germany and some other countries have laws prohibiting certain acts, such as dancing and horse racing, that are seen as profaning the solemn nature of the day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petre_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Petre-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stevens_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stevens-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Australia_and_New_Zealand">
        Australia and New Zealand
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Australia and New Zealand">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Good Friday is a holiday under state and territory laws in all states and territories in Australia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Generally speaking, shops in all Australian states (but not in the two territories of the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">
        Northern Territory
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">
        Australian Capital Territory
       </a>
       ) are required to remain closed for the duration of Good Friday, although there are certain shops which are permitted to open and other shops can apply for exemptions. All schools and universities close on Good Friday in Australia, and Good Friday falls within the school holidays in most years in all states and territories except the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">
        Northern Territory
       </a>
       , although many states now commence their school holidays in early April regardless of Easter. In 2018, for example, when Good Friday will fall on 30 March, only
       <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">
        Queensland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">
        Victoria
       </a>
       will have school holidays which coincide with Good Friday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australia.gov.au/about-australia/special-dates-and-events/school-term-dates_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-australia.gov.au/about-australia/special-dates-and-events/school-term-dates-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The vast majority of businesses are closed on Good Friday, although many recreational businesses, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Royal_Easter_Show" title="Sydney Royal Easter Show">
        Sydney Royal Easter Show
       </a>
       , open on Good Friday as among non-religious families Good Friday is a popular day to indulge in such activities. In New Zealand, Good Friday is a legal holiday
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is a day of mandatory school closure for all New Zealand state and integrated schools.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Good Friday is also a restricted trading day in New Zealand, which means that unexempted shops are not permitted to open on this day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">
        Canada
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Canada">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_(2010).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3052" data-file-width="2448" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg/220px-Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg/330px-Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg/440px-Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_%282010%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apokathylosis_-_Annunciation_Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_Toronto_(2010).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday#Vespers_of_Holy_and_Great_Friday" title="Good Friday">
          Vespers of Good Friday afternoon
         </a>
         , Greek Orthodox Cathedral in
         <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
          Toronto
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In Canada, Good Friday is a
       <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Canada" title="Public holidays in Canada">
        federal statutory holiday
       </a>
       . In the province of Quebec "employers can choose to give the day off either on Good Friday or Easter Monday."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuba">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In an online article posted on
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_News_Agency" title="Catholic News Agency">
        Catholic News Agency
       </a>
       by Alejandro Bermúdez on 31 March 2012,
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Cuba" title="President of Cuba">
        Cuban President
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro" title="Raúl Castro">
        Raúl Castro
       </a>
       , with the
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">
        Communist Party
       </a>
       and his advisers, decreed that Good Friday that year would be a holiday. This was Castro's response to a request made personally to him by
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">
        Pope Benedict XVI
       </a>
       during the latter's Apostolic Visitation to the island and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leon,_Mexico" title="Leon, Mexico">
        León
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       that month. The move followed the pattern of small advances in Cuba's relations with the Vatican, mirroring
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
        Pope John Paul II
       </a>
       's success in getting
       <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">
        Fidel Castro
       </a>
       to declare
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" title="Christmas Day">
        Christmas Day
       </a>
       a holiday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both Good Friday and Christmas are now
       <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Cuba" title="Public holidays in Cuba">
        annual holidays in Cuba
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       , despite the transfer of sovereignty from the UK to China in 1997, Good Friday continues to be a public holiday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Government offices, banks, post offices and most offices are closed on Good Friday.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">
        Ireland
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ireland">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">
        Republic of Ireland
       </a>
       , Good Friday is not an official public holiday, but most non-retail businesses close for the day. Up until 2018 it was illegal to sell alcoholic beverages on Good Friday, with some exceptions, so pubs and off-licences generally closed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ie-wheretolook_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ie-wheretolook-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Critics of the ban included the catering and tourism sector, but surveys showed that the general public were divided on the issue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent-goodfridayalcohol_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-independent-goodfridayalcohol-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">
        Northern Ireland
       </a>
       , a similar ban operates until 5 pm on Good Friday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-restrictionsni_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-restrictionsni-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">
        Malaysia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Malaysia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Although Malaysia is a
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">
        Muslim majority country
       </a>
       , Good Friday is declared as a public holiday in the states of
       <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">
        Sabah
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">
        Sarawak
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">
        East Malaysia
       </a>
       as there is a significant Christian indigenous population in both states.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">
        Malta
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Malta">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Holy Week commemorations reach their peak on Good Friday as the Roman Catholic Church celebrates the passion of Jesus. Solemn celebrations take place in all churches together with processions in different villages around
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">
        Gozo
       </a>
       . During the celebration, the narrative of the passion is read in some localities, while the Adoration of the Cross follows. Good Friday processions take place in
       <a href="/wiki/Birgu" title="Birgu">
        Birgu
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bormla" title="Bormla">
        Bormla
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7axaq" title="Għaxaq">
        Għaxaq
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Luqa" title="Luqa">
        Luqa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mosta" title="Mosta">
        Mosta
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Naxxar" title="Naxxar">
        Naxxar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paola,_Malta" title="Paola, Malta">
        Paola
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Qormi" title="Qormi">
        Qormi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">
        Rabat
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Senglea" title="Senglea">
        Senglea
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">
        Valletta
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%BBebbu%C4%A1,_Malta" title="Żebbuġ, Malta">
        Żebbuġ (Città Rohan)
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBejtun" title="Żejtun">
        Żejtun
       </a>
       . Processions in Gozo will be in
       <a href="/wiki/Nadur" title="Nadur">
        Nadur
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Gozo" title="Victoria, Gozo">
        Victoria
       </a>
       (St. George and Cathedral),
       <a href="/wiki/Xag%C4%A7ra" title="Xagħra">
        Xagħra
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBebbu%C4%A1,_Gozo" title="Żebbuġ, Gozo">
        Żebbuġ, Gozo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Philippines">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the predominantly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Philippines" title="Roman Catholicism in the Philippines">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       , the day is commemorated with street processions, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Way_of_the_Cross" title="Way of the Cross">
        Way of the Cross
       </a>
       , the chanting of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pasyon" title="Pasyon">
         Pasyón
        </a>
       </i>
       , and performances of the
       <i>
        Senákulo
       </i>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passion_play" title="Passion play">
        Passion play
       </a>
       . Some devotees engage in self-
       <a href="/wiki/Flagellant" title="Flagellant">
        flagellation
       </a>
       and even have themselves
       <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_in_the_Philippines" title="Crucifixion in the Philippines">
        crucified
       </a>
       as expressions of penance despite health risks and strong disapproval from the Church.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Church bells are not rung and Masses are not celebrated, while television features movies, documentaries and other shows focused on the religious event and other topics related to the Catholic faith, broadcasting mostly religious content. Malls and shops are generally closed, as are restaurants as it is the second of three public holidays within the week.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After three o'clock in the afternoon (the time at which Jesus is traditionally believed to have died), the faithful venerate the cross in the local church and follow the procession of the Burial of Jesus. The image of the dead Christ is then laid in state to be venerated, and sometimes treated in accordance with local burial customs.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">
        Cebu
       </a>
       and many parts of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visayan_Islands" title="Visayan Islands">
        Visayan Islands
       </a>
       , people usually eat
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Binignit" title="Binignit">
         binignit
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Philippines#Merienda" title="Cuisine of the Philippines">
         biko
        </a>
       </i>
       as a form of
       <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">
        fasting
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">
        Spain
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Spain">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nazarenosblancos.jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nazarenosblancos.jpg" title="Enlarge">

         </div>
         Nazarenos wearing
         <a href="/wiki/Capirote" title="Capirote">
          capirotes
         </a>
         , in
         <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">
          Málaga
         </a>
         , Spain
        </div>

       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Valladolid" title="Holy Week in Valladolid">

       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Viveiro" title="Holy Week in Viveiro">
        Holy Week in Viveiro
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Zamora" title="Holy Week in Zamora">
        Holy Week in Zamora
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">

          </b>
          <small>

           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>

            (February 2017)
           </i>
          </small>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hot_cross_bun.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hot_cross_bun.jpg/220px-Hot_cross_bun.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hot_cross_bun.jpg/330px-Hot_cross_bun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hot_cross_bun.jpg/440px-Hot_cross_bun.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hot_cross_bun.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hot_cross_bun" title="Hot cross bun">
          Hot cross buns
         </a>
         are traditionally toasted and eaten on Good Friday in Britain and Australia.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
          <a href="#cite_note-73">
           [73]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">
        UK
       </a>
       , Good Friday was historically a common law holiday and is recognised as an official public holiday
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (also known as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_Holiday" title="Bank Holiday">
        Bank Holiday
       </a>
       ). All state schools are closed and most businesses treat it as a holiday for staff; however, many retail stores now remain open.
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Civil_Service" title="Northern Ireland Civil Service">
        Government
       </a>
       services in Northern Ireland operate as normal on Good Friday, substituting
       <a href="/wiki/Easter_Tuesday" title="Easter Tuesday">
        Easter Tuesday
       </a>
       for the holiday.
      </p>
      <p>
       There has traditionally been no horse racing on Good Friday in the UK. However, in 2008, betting shops and stores opened for the first time on this day
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in 2014 Lingfield Park and Musselburgh staged the UK's first Good Friday race meetings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">
        BBC
       </a>
       has for many years introduced its 7 am News broadcast on
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">
        Radio 4
       </a>
       on Good Friday with a verse from
       <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Watts" title="Isaac Watts">
        Isaac Watts
       </a>
       ' hymn "
       <a href="/wiki/When_I_Survey_the_Wondrous_Cross" title="When I Survey the Wondrous Cross">
        When I Survey the Wondrous Cross
       </a>
       ".
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
        United States
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: United States">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       , Good Friday is not a government holiday at the federal level; however, individual states, counties and municipalities may observe the holiday. Good Friday is a state holiday in
       <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">
        Connecticut
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">
        Delaware
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
        Florida
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
        Hawaii
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">
        Indiana
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">
        Kentucky
       </a>
       (half day),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">
        North Carolina
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">
        North Dakota
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">
        Tennessee
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       State and local government offices and courts are closed, as well as some banks and post offices in these states, and in those counties and municipalities where Good Friday is observed as a holiday. Good Friday is also a holiday in the U.S. territories of
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">
        U.S. Virgin Islands
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The stock markets are closed on Good Friday
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but the foreign exchange and bond trading markets open for a partial business day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most retail stores remain open, while some of them may close early. Public schools and universities are often closed on Good Friday, either as a holiday of its own, or as part of
       <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">
        spring break
       </a>
       . The postal service operates, and banks regulated by the federal government do not close for Good Friday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In some governmental contexts Good Friday has been referred to by a generic name such as "spring holiday".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1999, in the case of
       <i>
        Bridenbaugh v. O'Bannon
       </i>
       , an Indiana state employee sued the governor for giving state employees Good Friday as a day off. The US Seventh Circuit Court of Appeals ruled against the plaintiff, stating that the government could give state employees a paid day off when that day is a religious holiday, including Good Friday, but only so long as the state can provide a valid secular purpose that coincides with the obvious religious purpose of the holiday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Calculating_the_date">
        Calculating the date
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Calculating the date">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Date_of_Easter" title="Date of Easter">
        Date of Easter
       </a>
      </div>
      <table border="1" cellpadding="6" cellspacing="0" style="float:right; margin-left:15px;">
       <caption style='"padding-left:'>
        <b>
         Dates for Good Friday, 2015–2030

       </tr>

        </td>

         26 April

      </table>
      <p>
       Good Friday is the Friday before Easter, which is calculated differently in
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">
        Eastern Christianity
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">
        Western Christianity
       </a>
       (see
       <a href="/wiki/Computus" title="Computus">
        Computus
       </a>
       for details). Easter falls on the first Sunday following the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paschal_Full_Moon" title="Paschal Full Moon">
        Paschal Full Moon
       </a>
       , the full moon on or after 21 March, taken to be the date of the vernal
       <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">
        equinox
       </a>
       . The Western calculation uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">
        Gregorian calendar
       </a>
       , while the Eastern calculation uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">
        Julian calendar
       </a>
       , whose 21 March now corresponds to the Gregorian calendar's 3 April. The calculations for identifying the date of the full moon also differ. See
       <a href="/wiki/Computus" title="Computus">
        Computus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In Eastern Christianity, Easter can fall between 22 March and 25 April on Julian Calendar (thus between 4 April and 8 May in terms of the Gregorian calendar, during the period 1900 and 2099), so Good Friday can fall between 20 March and 23 April, inclusive (or between 2 April and 6 May in terms of the Gregorian calendar).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_references">
        Cultural references
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cultural references">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Good Friday assumes a particular importance in the plot of
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">
        Richard Wagner
       </a>
       's music drama
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Parsifal" title="Parsifal">
         Parsifal
        </a>
       </i>
       , which contains an orchestral interlude known as the "Good Friday Music".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_from_non-observers">
        Criticism from non-observers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Criticism from non-observers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">
        Baptist
       </a>
       congregations,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Church_of_God" title="Philadelphia Church of God">
        Philadelphia Church of God
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Christianity" title="Non-denominational Christianity">
        non-denominational
       </a>
       churches oppose the observance of Good Friday, regarding it as a
       <a href="/wiki/Papist" title="Papist">
        papist
       </a>
       tradition, and instead observe the
       <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion" title="Crucifixion">
        Crucifixion
       </a>
       on Wednesday to coincide with the Jewish sacrifice of the
       <a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">
        Passover
       </a>
       Lamb (which Christians believe is an Old Testament pointer to Jesus Christ). A Wednesday Crucifixion of Jesus allows for him to be in the tomb ("heart of the earth") for three days and three nights as he told the Pharisees he would be (
       <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">
        Matthew
       </a>
       12:40), rather than two nights and a day (by
       <a href="/wiki/Counting#Inclusive_counting" title="Counting">
        inclusive counting
       </a>
       , as was the norm at that time) if he had died on a Friday.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Preparation Day (14
       <a href="/wiki/Nisan" title="Nisan">
        Nisan
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_calendar" title="Hebrew calendar">
        Hebrew calendar
       </a>
       ) – which is the day before Passover (15 Nisan), instead of the Friday morning as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synoptic_Gospel" title="Synoptic Gospel">
        Synoptic Gospels
       </a>
       refer to the sabbath and they believe this refers to a "high sabbath" which occurs on feast days, and not the ordinary weekly sabbath.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
        See also
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Good_Friday&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
       <ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
        <li style="display:table-row">
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P_christianity.svg">
           <img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="400" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/31px-P_christianity.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/47px-P_christianity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/P_christianity.svg/62px-P_christianity.svg.png 2x" width="31"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle">

            By many Lutherans Good Friday is observed as a strict fast. The lessons on Ash Wednesday emphasize the proper idea of the fast. The Sundays in Lent receive their names from the first words of their Introits in the Latin service, Invocavit, Reminiscere, Oculi, Lcetare, Judica.

           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080502234831/http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/john_paul_ii/letters/2000/documents/hf_jp-ii_let_20001021_riparatrici_en.html" rel="nofollow">

           <i>

           . 27 September 2000. Archived from
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/john_paul_ii/letters/2000/documents/hf_jp-ii_let_20001021_riparatrici_en.html" rel="nofollow">

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Vatican+archives&amp;rft.atitle=Letter+of+the+Holy+Father+John+Paul+II+to+Cardinal+Fiorenzo+Angelini+for+the+50th+Anniversary+of+the+Benedictine+Sisters+of+Reparation+of+the+Holy+Face&amp;rft.date=2000-09-27&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.vatican.va%2Fholy_father%2Fjohn_paul_ii%2Fletters%2F2000%2Fdocuments%2Fhf_jp-ii_let_20001021_riparatrici_en.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGood+Friday">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>

        <li id="cite_note-GassmannOldenburg2011-47">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-GassmannOldenburg2011_47-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-GassmannOldenburg2011_47-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation book">
           Gassmann, Günther; Oldenburg, Mark W. (10 October 2011).
           <i>
            Historical Dictionary of Lutheranism
           </i>
           . Scarecrow Press. p. 229.
           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
            ISBN
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780810874824" title="Special:BookSources/9780810874824">
            9780810874824
           </a>
           .
           <q>
            In many Lutheran churches, the Sundays during the Lenten season are called by the first word of their respective Latin Introitus (with the exception of Palm/Passion Sunday): Invocavit, Reminiscere, Oculi, Laetare, and Judica. Many Lutheran church orders of the 16th century retained the observation of the Lenten fast, and Lutherans have observed this season with a serene, earnest attitude. Special days of eucharistic communion were set aside on Maundy Thursday and Good Friday.
           </q>
          </cite>

           </span>

         <span class="reference-text">
          In addition to holidays where offices are closed, Texas also has "partial staffing holidays" (where offices are required to be open for public business, but where employees may take it off as a holiday) and "optional holidays" (where an employee may take off in lieu of taking off on a partial staffing holiday; Good Friday is an optional holiday).

                 (federal) = federal holidays, (state) = state holidays, (religious) = religious holidays, (week) = weeklong holidays, (month) = monthlong holidays, (36) =
                 <a href="/wiki/Title_36_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 36 of the United States Code">
                  Title 36 Observances and Ceremonies
                 </a>

                  Bold
                 </b>
                 indicates major holidays commonly celebrated in the United States, which often represent the major celebrations of the month.
